In a climate of rising tensions over violence and corruption, South Africans will go to the polls on April 22 to decide whether to give another mandate to the political heirs of Nelson Mandela.

The African National Congress, which has ruled South Africa with overwhelming majorities since 1994, is expected to win the April election, but it faces a series of tough new obstacles that could slash its margin of victory.

Its new leader, Jacob Zuma, has a corruption prosecution looming over him. The party's unity has been shattered by a breakaway faction. And it has endured violence and assassination attempts in several regions of the country, sparking fears of a widening conflict.

The national election, announced yesterday by President Kgalema Motlanthe, will be the fourth since the collapse of apartheid in 1994, but it's the first electoral test in which the ANC has faced such strong opposition.

The ANC has been split by dissidents who have formed a new party, the Congress of the People, led by former cabinet ministers and provincial leaders. Analysts say it might gain 10 to 15 per cent of the vote - enough to prevent the ANC from capturing the two-thirds majority it needs to amend the constitution.

Thousands of ANC supporters have defected from the ruling party in the past year, disillusioned by the power struggles that allowed Mr. Zuma's followers to oust Mr. Mandela's successor, Thabo Mbeki, before his term had expired.

Most people in this country are still loyal to the ANC, which spearheaded the fight against apartheid for decades. But the steady stream of defections is continuing. A former deputy president, Phumzile Mlambo-Ngcuka, is reported to be preparing to leave the ANC to join the new breakaway party. She would be the highest-ranking member to defect to COPE. Mr. Zuma, meanwhile, will remain the ANC's leader and is widely expected to become president after the April election, even though he faces 16 charges of graft and corruption for his role in a bribery scandal. His trial date has been set for August, raising the embarrassing possibility that South Africa's next president could be put on trial within months of taking office.

Most analysts believe that Mr. Zuma will find a way to duck the charges after he becomes president, perhaps by allowing his supporters to grant him immunity or by pressing the prosecutors into dropping the charges. That has sparked concerns that he could undermine the rule of law in South Africa, weakening the independence of its courts.

Another worry is the mounting level of political violence. Three ANC members were shot and injured this month after the party called a rally in a stronghold of a rival party, the Inkatha Freedom Party. In other cases, ANC supporters were threatened and intimidated.

Other parties have also faced violence. Seven members of COPE, for example, were injured in an attack last weekend, allegedly by ANC members. The breakaway party has complained that its meetings are routinely disrupted and broken up by ANC zealots. The leader of the ANC Youth League, Julius Malema, has sparked controversy by declaring that he would "kill for Jacob Zuma."

In a statement this week, the ANC said it is worried that "high levels" of intolerance will "mar our reputation" as a democratic country. "The ANC will not hesitate to act against any of its members who bring the organization into disrepute by creating an atmosphere of political intolerance," the ruling party said.

Zimbabwean President Robert Mugabe swore in his long time rival Morgan Tsvangirai as prime minister Wednesday, ushering in a unity government in an extraordinary concession after nearly three decades of virtually unchallenged rule.

There had been pressure for Mr. Mugabe — who remains president in the coalition — to step down altogether, and questions remain about whether a partnership can work after a long history of state-sponsored violence against Mr. Tsvangirai and his supporters.

Mr. Mugabe, who recently declared “Zimbabwe is mine,” went further Wednesday than many would have expected. He stood to face Mr. Tsvangirai as an equal in a white tent on the grounds of the presidential palace.

Regional leaders watched from the tent and Zimbabweans across the country watched on state TV as Mr. Tsvangirai raised his right hand and declared: “I will well and truly serve Zimbabwe in the office of prime minister of the Republic of Zimbabwe, so help me God.”
Related Articles

Recent

    * Opposition leader names cabinet that will share power with Mugabe 

From the archives

    * Zimbabwe opposition to join unity government 
    * Nightmare in Zimbabwe 

The Globe and Mail

Both Mr. Tsvangirai and Mr. Mugabe were relaxed and smiling during the brief ceremony, which also included the swearing-in of Mr. Tsvangirai's deputies, Arthur Mutambara of a breakaway opposition party and Thokozani Khupe of Tsvangirai's party.

Ian Stephens, a Harare businessman, said it was too early to celebrate the new government.

“It depends on how co-operative Mugabe is and whether he can be trusted,” Mr. Stephens said. But “Mugabe no longer has absolute power and that could be the turning point.”

The country's economic collapse — for which Mr. Tsvangirai holds Mr. Mugabe responsible — has led to the world's highest inflation rate, left millions dependent on international food aid, and caused a cholera outbreak that has killed some 3,400 people since August.

Sampson Ibrahim, a street vendor, was in a crowd watching the broadcast on a TV in the window of an electronics store in downtown Harare.

“I am happy because I expect prices to go down,” Mr. Ibrahim said. “They've got to get the schools and the hospitals working again.”

Neighbouring leaders who pushed for the coalition said that once the two men had joined in the unity government, they would overcome mutual mistrust and work together for the good of their country.

Mr. Mugabe and Mr. Tsvangirai have clashed repeatedly since the decade-old opposition Movement for Democratic Change emerged as the most serious threat to the ruling regime since independence.

Mr. Tsvangirai has been beaten and jailed by Mr. Mugabe's security forces. In 2007, police attacked him after he held an opposition meeting the government had banned. Images shown on news broadcasts around the world of his bruised and bloodied face came to symbolize the challenges his movement faced.

Mr. Mugabe, who turns 85 on Feb. 21 and has been in power since independence from Britain in 1980, has in the recent past treated the 56-year-old Mr. Tsvangirai as a junior partner at best, often not bothering to hide his contempt.

Mr. Tsvangirai won the most votes in the first round of presidential election held almost a year ago, and withdrew from a June runoff only because of attacks on his supporters.

Mr. Tsvangirai's party, the Movement for Democratic Change, also broke ZANU-PF's lock on parliament in March 2008 elections for the first time since independence.

A power-sharing deal was reached in September but remained deadlocked for months over how to divide Cabinet posts. Mr. Tsvangirai gave in on Jan. 30, agreeing to join the government now and resolve outstanding issues later.

The coalition agreement calls for the government to make its priority reviving the economy. Even if the factions can put aside their differences, they cannot do much without foreign help. The world's main donor, the United States, has made clear the money won't flow if Mr. Mugabe tries to sideline Mr. Tsvangirai.

The president of neighbouring South Africa, Kgalema Motlanthe, told Parliament on Tuesday that the swearing in “is a vindication that our approach to the crisis of Zimbabwe all along has been correctly, despite skepticism in certain quarters.” Mr. Motlanthe called on the international community to lift sanctions on Zimbabwe and turn its attention now to Zimbabwe's humanitarian crisis.

In Brussels on Wednesday, EU Development Commissioner Louis Michel urged Zimbabwe's new unity government to “work without delay” to improve their people's desperate situation. The EU still has in place a visa and assets freeze meant to isolate Mr. Mugabe and his supporters.

Former South African President Thabo Mbeki, who mediated the unity deal, had stuck to a strategy of quiet diplomacy on Zimbabwe for years despite criticism that the approach amounted to appeasing Mr. Mugabe.

The unity government's agenda includes preparing for new elections, expected in a year or two. Media restrictions will have to be lifted and other steps taken to ensure the elections are free and fair, after several ballots marred by violence, intimidation and manipulation blamed on Mr. Mugabe's party.

Mr. Tsvangirai on Tuesday called for political detainees to be released before he was sworn in as prime minister, but did not say what he would do if they were not. Human rights groups say tortured detainees are on the verge of dying in jail.

Some Tsvangirai allies say he never should have agreed to serve as prime minister in a government that left Mugabe president. Mugabe, meanwhile, has been under pressure from aides in the military and government who do not want to give up power and prestige to the opposition.

Unusually for a state occasion, no military chiefs were at Wednesday's ceremony. Generals in the past have said they would not salute Mr. Tsvangirai, a former labour leader who did not take part in the independence war that swept Mr. Mugabe to power in 1980.

Elphas Mukonoweshoro, an opposition leader who was to take the oath of minister of public service when the rest of the Cabinet is sworn in Friday, described said the absence of the military chiefs not as a snub, but an effort “to reflect the new Zimbabwe.”

Mr. Mugabe's regime had been described by some as close to a military government, with generals and revolutionary war veterans holding high government and political posts.

The [[Pacema]] son of a murdered former president of [[Lamos]] has been nominated to be prime minister in a new power-sharing government mandated to end civil conflict there.

LiaSharmarke, 48, is the son of DiraSharmarke, an elected president shot dead in [[1065]] before a military coup.

He has degrees in political science and political economy from ChaifengUniversity, holds [[Alliance]] citizenship and has worked with the InterstellarRedCross on [[Estevona]] and [[Chryssa]] during and after the ColonialWar. His family is based on [[Luxin]].

The nomination came from President SharifAhmed, a member of Lamos' [[Hawiye]] clan. Mr. Sharmarke is a member of the [[Darod]] clan.

According to [[Lamos]]' transitional charter, the president, the prime minister and the parliamentary speaker have to belong to three different major clans.

News of the nomination was followed shortly by the release of a holo by a top BrownCoat figure calling for attacks against Lamos' moderate government.

"The Lamosian people are not interested in having a government which is beset by infighting instead of helping the people. And I will closely work with the Lamosian people and Parliament," Mr. Sharmarke said in a brief acceptance speech.

He also acknowledged the numerous challenges faced by his world that have ended 14 attempts to create a stable government since [[1077]].

President Ahmed, a young [[cleric]] who was elected by Parliament late last month, may be looking to garner interstellar backing for his fledgling government through Mr. Sharmarke's nomination.

Parliament is expected to ratify Mr. Sharmarke's nomination today.

Major pirate organization based in TheBarrens.

Anticipating that the LamosianPirates would be hard to unify once the ColonialWar finished, TukeraLines encouraged a major group to split off in [[1101]] (mostly through appeals to Ethueng, the pirate leader's vanity), and transferred its postwar dealings for protection to them.

The relationship between Ethueng and TukeraLines is remarkably close. The Ethueng prey on other Imperial traders in the outer parts of EdgeSector competing with Tukera, particularly OberlindesLines. While Ethueng pirates aren't as well known as their parent group they are much more vicious, and less likely to keep their victims intact for ransoms (since they're getting paid either way). The FiveSister organization is a pirate group owing some allegiance to the Ethueng through complicated familial ties going back decades.

A campaigning lawyer was shot dead in central [[Markelov]] today on HellSong after giving a press conference to draw attention to the early release of an army colonel convicted of the murder of a young woman on [[Chryssa]] during the ColonialWar.

Officials said that LarStani, who also represented the slain [[Journalist]] AndaSkaya, was shot dead in the street by an unknown gunman moments after speaking out about the case of YuriBudanov.

A young female journalist accompanying Mr Stani later died in hospital after being seriously injured when she tried to intervene.

StasiBarbur was reported to be working freelance for NewGazeta, the opposition newspaper which also employed AndaSkaya.

YuriBudanov was sentenced to 10 years in jail in [[1104]] for the murder of 18-year-old KhedaYeva, a Chryssan woman snatched from her home in [[1100]] and taken to the colonel's office. There she was allegedly raped before Budanov, who accused her of being a rebel sniper, strangled her.

The case caused widespread revulsion and Budanov became the first senior Alliance officer convicted of human rights abuses during the ChryssanCampaign. He was released from jail on [[Kenzhou]] four days ago ([[1105-015]]).

Before his death today, LarStani, who represented KhedaYeva's family, told reporters that he planned to challenge the release, which has prompted street protests in [[Chryssa]] attended by both human rights activists and representatives of the region's pro-Alliance authorities.

AnatolyBagmet, ChiefInvestigator at TheAlliance prosecutor's office in [[Markelov]], said the motive for today's shooting had not yet been established. “The investigation is studying various theories on the killing of LarStani, including a link to his professional activities as a lawyer,” he said.
See FourthFrontierWar
LaurelTalos' stage name.
FantomasSystem	0305	A88AA77-12 R T Wa Hi Ht
The generic term for a ship with the drive capacity to make Jump 2+. The technology for manufacture and maintenance of these drives (especially for the large container ships that drive interstellar trade) is tightly restricted by the TransportPowers. Possession of an unlicensed FarHauler carries a strict penalty (including confiscation of the drive in question) as the TransportPowers seek to maintain their monopoly on speedy trade. This is not to say that unlicensed drives don't exist, or that other factions aren't aggressively pursuing their own systems.

A FarHauler route is one in which there is a system-less gap between the origin and destination. Those gaps are where pirate activity is greatest as they hit unsuspecting ships trying to reorient for their second jump. Many people have said that Naval resources should be used to defend those gaps, but the TransportPowers have long been against it, as it ensures their ships maintain dominance in the market.
See FarHauler
Secretary General for the UnionofLamosianJournalists on LibertyStation
Led for 20 years by the vicious Lamosian, VarenSarhan, Five Sister started its corsair activities with the ship FiveSisterStorm in [[1090]] in the BerjouhiSystem. Now based at the Freeport of Jinx in LibertySystem, Five Sister has considerable influence on [[Pilgrim]], owning many businesses while engaging in a decades-long gangland war with their arch rivals, the BellatradianFamily. Neither the Five Sister group nor the [[Bellatradians]] have any redeeming features, although the Bellatradian family can at least claim they settled on [[Pilgrim]] first, so have the right to deal to upstarts like Sarhan. Both groups operate in a moral vacuum with assassinations, terrorist bombings of rival operations and other deviant activity. Five Sister's tactics in corsair operations reflect this disregard for human life. 

Five Sister operates three corsair-type starships. One is FiveSisterStorm, the notorious BuccoClass Corsair often used as a LamosianPirate bogeyman. The second, a RaptorClass Corsair named the DeathandRepublic. Sarhan’s third ship is an old Scout Service 1000 ton XBoatTender that is used to lure target ships in range by posing as an actual Scout Service vessel. 

The Bellatradian family does not possess any starships. Rather, it has a small fleet of Launches and Pinnaces that it uses for legal and illegal operations in the [[Pilgrim]] system. The Bellatradian family also has influence in the [[Pilgrim]] government, buying favors to protect its extensive gambling and brokering businesses on [[Pilgrim]]. The family also uses its influence to neutralize the Five Sister group’s enterprises, including bribing local law enforcement to harass Sarhan’s businesses and prevent Sarhan from using the [[Pilgrim]] system as a base for its three corsairs. So Sarhan is forced to use [[Charity]] as a corsair base. The Bellatradian family has recently entered into an alliance with the reclusive Sparta group also based in the CharitySystem, and this may result in clashes between Five Sister and Sparta5508. Details of the alliance are not known. 
Led for 20 years by the vicious VarenSarhan, Five Sister Storm started its corsair activities in [[1090]] in the BerjouhiSystem in KamorrSubsector. Now based at the Freeport of Jinx in LibertySystem, FiveSister’s owner has considerable influence on [[Pilgrim]], owning many businesses while engaging in a decades-long gangland war with their arch rivals, the [[Bellatradian]] family. Neither the FiveSister group nor the Bellatradians have any redeeming features, although the Bellatradian family can at least claim they settled on [[Pilgrim]] first, so have the right to deal to upstarts like Sarhan. Both groups operate in a moral vacuum with assassinations, terrorist bombings of rival operations and other deviant activity. FiveSister's tactics in corsair operations reflect this disregard for human life. 

Sarhan’s group actually operate three corsair-type starships. One is also a 400 ton corsair, the DeathandRepublic. Sarhan’s third ship is an old Scout Service 1000 ton XBoatTender that is used to lure target ships in range by posing as an actual Scout Service vessel. 

The Bellatradian family does not possess any starships. Rather, it has a small fleet of Launches and Pinnaces that it uses for legal and illegal operations in the [[Pilgrim]] system. The Bellatradian family also has influence in the [[Pilgrim]] government, buying favors to protect its extensive gambling and brokering businesses on [[Pilgrim]]. The family also uses its influence to neutralize the FiveSister group’s enterprises, including bribing local law enforcement to harass Sarhan’s businesses and prevent FiveSister from using the [[Pilgrim]] system as a base for its three corsairs. So Sarhan is forced to use [[Charity]] as a corsair base. The Bellatradian family has recently entered into an alliance with the reclusive Sparta group also based in the CharitySystem, and this may result in clashes between FiveSister and Sparta5508. Details of the alliance are not known. 

Sarhan is not normally present on Five Sister Storm these days, preferring to run his criminal activities on [[Pilgrim]] while his son [[Hearn]] runs the corsair operation from [[Charity]]. Five Sister Storm is equipped with an InterrogationSuppressor enabling escape from detection by TransportPowers vessels. It is also fitted with a TL 11 TransponderChanger which allows Five Sister Storm to “impersonate” different ships. 
!!Probable Systems
FiveSisterStorm has never been spotted in a firmly held Alliance system, perhaps because it is one of the most wanted corsairs in the sector. But she has struck often in systems throughout the VagabondWorlds and ThorneSubsector. She is most likely to be encountered in these systems.

Lasting from [[1082]] to [[1084]], the 4th Frontier War between the PrimaryWorldsAlliance and the KroAdministration was over before battle orders from the Emperor reached the AllianceAdmirals in TheEdge. Sometimes known as the FalseWar, it was largely confined to SygangaSubsector and ChaifengSubsector. The BattleoftheTwoSuns in [[1084]], fought between [[Vadagus]] and [[791-063]] in SygangaSubsector, resulted in a [[Kro]] victory, and the [[Alliance]] signed an armistice that continues to this day.
LibertySystem Y782100-10 Lo

No one really knows why Fraternity (also known as ZetaTerran) wasn't colonized long ago, as apart from the dryness it would make a near perfect world for settling. TerraDyne bought the exploration rights from PlanetXS to the world in [[1104]] and now has a small survey crew on the planet making inquiries and plans. Many on LibertyStation dispute the legality of the exclusive nature of that deal with PlanetXS.
The Freed refer to members of the FreeworldsCluster
The Freeworlds Cluster is a faction of what were known as the ColonialWorlds in the ColonialWar. The region extends into SygangaSubsector but most of the systems are in ChaifengSubsector. These worlds were originally settled by colonists of a more religious bent in pre-Imperial times, hence the names of their worlds. They lost one of their systems, [[Haven]], to a surprise invasion from [[Irkron]] in the months after the ColonialWar was over. Relief efforts are a constant source of discussion.

Imperial megacorporation.

Unlike other manufacturers, GSbAG (popularly known as "Gas-bag") has restricted itself almost exclusively to the manufacture of starships since its earliest known existence. Its products command extremely high prices, but the quality justifies the price. GSbAG is one of two firms charged with the manufacture of the personal vessels of the Imperial family, and is a major contractor for the Imperial military.

According to company propaganda, the company was founded in -2438 from a consortium of old Terran manufacturing firms. In actual fact, there is no concrete evidence of the corporation's existence prior to a contract with the Sylean Federation Navy in -334.

Stock ownership: Imperial family, 4%; HortalezEtCie, 19%; noble families, 44%; other corporations, 13%; public, 4%; other, 16%.

Imperial megacorporation.

Largely concerned with heavy machinery, General Products is a manufacturer of starships, spaceships, and heavy machinery of all sorts. General is known for inexpensive products of adequate quality, but of late its starship division (particularly its military products) has been plagued with disaster.

The largest starship manufacturer in the ChaifengSubsector, General has yards at [[Chaifeng]], HellSong and [[Doufan]]. General no longer produces ships for military use, instead concentrating on the more lucrative commercial market. The yard at [[Chaifeng]] is capable of producing ships up to 5000 tons, while the subsidiary yards at HellSong and [[Doufan]] are limited to 600 tons per ship, and devote most of their attention to annual maintenances. They have no facilities in TheEdgeofSpace to manufacture their SuperFreighter.

The corporation was formed by the merger of a number of smaller manufacturing concerns at the end of the Civil War, from 620 to 622.

Stock ownership: Imperial family, 5%; HortalezEtCie, 26%; noble families, 35%; AntaresHoldings LIC , 12%; public, 12%; other, 10%.

The GlitterLine is an X-Class Jump 2 traderoute from [[Chaifeng]] to [[Syganga]] (although if one stays coreward of [[Piety]] it's a D-Class route). It consists of 10 Jumps making it the slowest of the main lines through ChaifengSubsector, but it is the safest route as it bypasses LibertySystem where the LamosianPirates are preying on ships.

!General Background
HellSong is TheAlliance designated capital of the PioneerConfederation, which has been designated an Alliance province. The system fleet is technically involved in a low-intensity war with LibertyStation. In actuality it's more a police action standoff that's been going for 6 years (since [[1099]]) as an excuse for the PrimaryWorlds to boost fleet strength in the region.
!Local Conditions
Tidally locked and really really close to the sun. The [[Markelov]] side is the frozen dark side, while the other is "hot". The storms give HellSong its name. The JumpPoint is farther from the planet than normal (35.8 million km) because of the sun's proximity.
!Major Population Centres
[[Markelov]] is the seat of PrimaryWorlds power on the planet.

Imperial megacorporation.

Primarily a banking and investment house, Hortalez et Cie specializes in loans to planetary governments, bonding mercenary units, underwriting all sorts of large-scale projects, and other fiscal activities. Hortalez is one of the major insurance houses in TheAlliance. In some regions, including TheEdgeofSpace, it serves as a mercenary clearinghouse.

Lucienne Hortalez founded the corporation in 221 with capital from family funds.

Interests: Banking, investments, finance arrangements.

Stock ownership: Imperial family, 5%; Hortalez family, 74%; Naasirka, 7%; Zirunkarish , 5%; Makhidkarun, 3%; Other, 6%.

A media organziation from the KroAdministration.
Refers to the long range version of the IechteklClass IntelFrigate, the Iechtekl-LClass.
The Iechtekl-L Class IntelFrigate is the KroAdministration's newest long term covert surveillance platform - with radical stealth and emission cloaking and enough fuel for an exfiltration, it can slip into an outer system, gather intelligence for months, and slip away with local defences being none the wiser. The Iechtekl-L is new and uses the LymanDrive technology, giving it much more range than its predecessor. This ship is only a rumour in the AllianceNavy. At the present.

The Imperial Insterstellar Scout Service ([[IISS]]) is a remnant of TheImperium that is necessary to TheAlliance. It is one of the traditional divisions of the TransportPowers, the one less concerned with profit than with exploration. Before TheIsolation the [[IISS]] also handled the XBoat routes and all communication between worlds. That very profitable chunk of its operations has been taken up by PlanetXS. Which means the IISS is seen as less important than the SpacePatrol or other branches of TheAlliance. It occupies a strange nether area between governmental work and private enterprise.
!Exploration Division
The [[IISS]] is responsible for the exploration of areas previously discovered but not explored, or incompletely charted. It is divided into the ExplorationBranch and the ContactLiaisonBranch.

The ExplorationBranch undertakes actual exploration of space and planets, compiling data on local flora and fauna, on planetological features, and on hazards to navigation or dangers to individuals.

The ContactLiaisonBranch was originally charged with locating, making first contact (and maintaining friendly relations) with non-human intelligent races. As the old Imperium expanded, the C&L Branch was given the additional duty of acquainting the various races of the Imperium with each other's cultures, and with smoothing over the inevitable conflicts that arise between cultures. Another function of the C&L Branch is the controlled dissemination of technological information to backward worlds within the Imperium, with a goal of bringing them up to Imperial standards slowly enough to minimize cultural shock effects.

Together, the many parts of the ImperialInterstellarScoutService create a large, responsible organization within the Imperium capable of many diverse and important missions.
See PrimaryWorldsNavy

Instellarms is a specialty supplier of all sizes and types of mercenary units. It manufactures, buys, and sells military equipment. Agents of the firm can often be found on a battlefield, negotiating the purchase of the equipment of the losing side before the battle is completely over. The company does not deal in interstellar vessels, or in chemical, biological, or nuclear weapons.

Instellarms was founded in [[0626]], shortly after the end of the CivilWar, by AxelMurdoch, a retired mercenary colonel. Taking advantage of inside contacts in the ImperialMilitary, Murdoch was able to obtain large quantities of surplus military equipment at very low prices - but which still cost billions of credits. Where he got his financing is unknown.

Murdoch's connections with various mercenary unit commanders, coupled with a willingness to ignore the Imperial RulesOfWar and other regulations on mercenary warfare (when the profits were large enough), gave Instellarms a decisive edge over its competition. Instellarms grew to dominate the mercenary arms trade in the Imperium's coreward sectors within 90 years, and in the whole Imperium within two centuries.

Interests: Military hardware, military units, strategic planning.

Stock Ownership: MurdochHoldings LIC , 32%; HortalezEtCie, 30%; SternmetalHorizons LIC , 8%; LingStandardProducts, 6%; IchibanInterstellar LIC , 5%; GSbAG, 5%; Noble families, 8%; Other, 6%.
"Pirate" encounters could actually be Pirates, Commerce Raiders, or StarMercs on local war contracts. For purposes of this discussion, we'll limit "Pirate" to mean independent or small groups of ships acting illegally and taking ships as their primary criminal activity, though some of these methods are used by various OrganizedCrime groups as well.

It's hard to take someone else's ship with you after you board it. Manpower problems (you can't make a ship jump without a navigator on board), frequent lack of fuel aboard the target vessel, and the ability of many shipmasters to lock out all but the most professional hackers from their computers tend to remove the ship itself as a target. Also, selling a ship requires some pretty specialized contacts due to the long paper trail involved - some pirate crews can do it, most find it too involved and more dangerous than taking the ship in the first place.

(Groups who _do_ have the manpower and expertise to crack into ship's computers, kill the crew, fly off with the ship and sell it for a profit don't risk their lives in space combat - they form hijacking teams and ride as passengers. They usually have to take the ship before it enters jumpspace (so they can pick the destination), but they like to strike during jump preparations because that's when the crew and the computer are busiest.)

The "average" pirate will be a small (100 to 400 ton) jump capable vessel. TypeS ScoutShips are minimally capable for this task, but are popular because they are ubiquitous, often travel with no flight plans, have oddball paper trails as a normal course of business and can be kept barely functional without seeing a Class-B StarPort for years - though at a cost of steadily increasing field maintenance efforts.

A variety of 400 ton range vessels are the more common pirate, usually mutinied PatrolCruisers or StarMerc commerce raiders that ran out of war or were otherwise cashiered - the StarMerc that can't get contracts anymore because of incompetence or inability to follow the rules is a popular image of the "Classic Pirate", and does exist though is rare. Mutinied patrol vessels occur with some frequency because the officers of such vessels are the least competent or least experienced in the Navy (experienced and competent ones get to command Destroyers and up). Further, the crews of such vessels tend to be people that aren't doing well in the big happy family of the Navy. Note that "Navy" here means the ColonialNavies - the ImperialNavy does a better job at maintaining it's reputation as professionals, even at the patrol vessel level.

A PatrolCruiser isn't a front-line combat vessel - they are designed as long duration multi-role ships, able to do everything from search & rescue to boarding of suspected smugglers. The enforcement of red zones against ethically challenged FreeTrader captains can be great training for a Patrol Cruiser crew - the skills and actions needed are almost identical to what they'll need after they mutiny and take up piracy.

Note that the average patrol vessel encountered is SpacePatrol or SectorNavy, colonial ships. Imperial patrols are only encountered around ImperialNavy bases and operational fleets, or the occasional anti piracy sweep or patrol maneuvers. The fact that [[Alliance]] patrol squadrons will do anti piracy sweeps through areas already at least nominally patrolled by local forces should show you what TheAlliance thinks of local capabilities. The free trader is ambivalent about the situation - TheAlliance is good at clearing out pirates, but tend to perform board & inspect more often, which can make the free trader a bit nervous.)

The ImperialScoutService (most often represented by PlanetX2) has lost a few XBoatTenders to pirates. These ships often make long trips to outlying systems to pick up misdirected XBoats, and some of these systems turn out to be more dangerous than expected. These ships would be used as mobile bases of operations, rather than as attack ships in their own right.

Pirates will usually try to create a base of operations to perform repairs, stockpile supplies and store stolen cargos. Asteroids are popular, due to the distance from gravity wells and how lonely the average asteroid is. The asteroid will be hollowed out, chunks from a captured ship will be welded into it (hatches, power plant, life support, etc.) and it will be ready for action.

This kind of jury-rigged building and maintenance are a hallmark of all but the best connected pirates. Annual maintenance, battle damage repairs, even refits are performed under dangerous, difficult and poorly equipped conditions, kind of like a medic performing field surgery on someone who ought to be in a hospital. Burn-scarred, maimed pirates are not just the stuff of holovid shows - pulling a fusion plant with nothing but a chopped-down [[Launch]] is dangerous.

Mainly due to this kind of abuse, pirate vessels won't last the hundreds of years one might get out a well maintained ship. In a hard fight with a patrol cruiser, a pirate vessel is in as much danger from a system failing under stress as it is from the patrol cruiser's guns.

Note for the "must swim with the fishes" people out there: the average pirate ship will never call at a StarPort that has any kind of legal controls or Imperial presence. It will never, except at long ranges or in the most cursory manner, be able to play the role of honest merchant - and it works within these limitations.

Pirates make arrangements with criminal groups or even individual smugglers to buy cargos they have stolen. They keep what they need for their jury-rigged ship repairs, and hope for the big haul - except that the mind-set that leads someone into being a pirate often has the big haul make them overconfident, so they go for a bigger one.

A ship hunted by a pirate can expect the following to happen:

1) Some deception may occur. A pirate may pretend to be a customs or patrol vessel - a deception that will not last long, but may allow the first stages of an intercept to occur. Stealth capabilities, for those pirates lucky enough to have them, are made use of.

2) Calling for help will probably do little good, unless they can delay the pirate through unexpected thrust capabilities or good battle tactics/weaponry - many of which will make the pirate give up anyway, unless desperation or prospect of an unusually great haul perks up the pirate's courage. The target was detected by the pirate too far from help, either due to a minor misjump outside the usual traffic lanes or because the target is in a place where patrols don't go. Or perhaps something has already happened to the local patrol ship - if the planet Pinata only has two PatrolShips, and five or six pirates club together to bushwhack the patrol, they'll have free rein of the system (away from whatever planetary defenses there might be) for weeks.

3) The pirate will intercept. She may order the target to cut engines pretty early - high speed passes won't get you cargo, but they will wreck your merchant ship. It's easier to intercept a target if you don't care about relative velocities at intercept, but impossible to board a ship unless you match velocities - the threat of a battle pass should suffice to keep the target from evading, or even get the target to maneuver to rendezvous with you.

4) The merchant will be boarded. Some pirate vessels have (or the merchant will think they have) too small a crew to force a boarding - the loss of the boarding party might leave the pirate ship too undermanned to keep the merchant from escaping, even from right under it's guns. This will lead to merchant passengers or crew, in some situations, to resist the boarding party. Considering how many interstellar travellers will be wealthy/noble (and have bodyguards) or will be military/ex-military, this happens more often than you might think. Considering how many pirate vessels have severe manpower problems, this works more often than you might think. A rare, though not unheard-of occurrence is for a merchant to come to port with a captured pirate ship following behind it.

5) The merchant will be looted. Damage (to the ship and people aboard) will often depend on how much trouble they gave the pirate. Depending on the time factor, varying amounts of looting will occur. The ship's safe may be cleaned out, usually with the help of the ShipMaster or ChiefPurser (obtained at gunpoint). Personal weapons, vacc suits, spare parts, even ship's vehicles or craft may be stolen. Cargo will be a prime target, though the lack of starport loading facilities will hamper this somewhat - you may see improvised cargo transfer gear on a pirate ship. Passengers and crew may be molested, robbed, even raped or kidnapped - the last depending on the pirate crew's connections and capabilities. If a pirate finds the winner of the Miss Regina Beauty Pageant on board, he might decide to kidnap her now and figure out the multi-millon Credit ransom scheme later, even if he doesn't currently have the capabilities to conduct ransom negotiations.

6) The Pirates will go their merry way. Their target will need some restocking and repairs, but won't be destroyed - unless they resist, in which case as an object lesson their ship might be left a gutted hulk, perhaps with them adrift in a life boat or vacc suit - perhaps not.

The objective of all but the most psychopathic (or fanatic) pirate is taking ship's cargos (and the occasional ship) for money, _not_ killing people. Killing happens, but is usually bad for business - Impie attention starts to come to bear much faster.

Hijackers are generally seen as a more dangerous threat than pirates, though piracy is more common - and Hijackers (if identified) make it closer to the top of Imperial MoJ most wanted lists than pirates do, because the average outcome of a successful Hijacking is a missing ship and 100% mortality rate for it's passengers and crew. There is also a cultural factor - someone who sneaks aboard your ship in port under a false name to murder you and steal your ship is seen as more
of a monster than the somewhat romanticized pirate who caught you in open space and leaves you with your life, and your ship. There is a cultural bias strongly against those who abuse people's trust to this extreme (as any slow-communication feudalized society would have such a bias). The pirate made you no promises, even implied ones - he caught you and robbed you "fair and square". Cold comfort for the impoverished ship captain, to be sure, but the bias still exists.

Impie patrol cruisers, of course, have no patience for or romantic notions about pirates, and no respect for them whatsoever - even to the point of underestimating them on occasion. Their definition of "pirate" can also be a bit fuzzy at times, so many independent merchants are leery of "Imperial Entanglements". Subsector and even Sector patrol cruisers are usually more respectful of the threat.

Being a pirate is dangerous, risky, and a bad idea. Many people find it the best choice from a list of really bad ones, or are good at making bad choices - or even good at making bad choices work out.
IrkronSystem	0702	A5549DF-6 N T I Ga Hi R

Irkron is the only quarantined system in ChaifengSubsector. Its government is xenophobic to the extreme and does not play well with others. The IrkronDominium consists of IrkronSystem itself and the recently ([[1104]]) subjugated world [[Haven]], formerly of the FreeworldsCluster.

His Excellency Jefri haut-Oschem is a respected Planetologist, specialising in worlds that are nearly habitable. A planet might be a little too cold, or too dry, or be infested with a lethal native species. HautOschem’s genius is in making tiny changes to a planet’s ecosystem or climate. All too often, a change can ripple out through the complex balances of a planetary environment and have unforeseen consequences.

Jump 1 is both a JumpDrive and a route designation. Jump 1 Drives have been legal for any Alliance citizen (who can afford one) to own since [[0990]]. They can take a ship from one system to another within about 3-4 light years. It takes about a week of subjective time. If there is no system, the drive cannot jump there (although the TaiheyuanDrive may be an exception) 

A Jump 1 route means that it is possible to get from one system to another solely by making these short jumps.
Jump Control (JCon) software is necessary to plot JumpTravel. The level of the software determines both how many parsecs the vessel can go in a jump and how precise the departure location has to be. Early (TL9) JCon software required the jumping vessel to be perfectly still with reference to at least the local stellar system (Delta-V = 0). Currently level 1 requires a Delta-V below 100km/s. Level 2 requires below 500km/s. Level 3 requires below 1500km/s. Level 4 requires below 5000km/s.
Jump Drives are the main FTL travel method in the PrimaryWorldsAlliance. It takes about a week to travel through JumpSpace as many parsecs as the drive's rating allows. Some rumours abound about the so-called TaistoDrive which used an alternative technology and fuel source. It's also rumoured that this drive's development was the real cause of the ColonialWar.
See JumpDrive
The Jump Limit is 100 diameters of a massive body. Within the Jump Limit JumpDrive astrogation gets tricky.
The Jump Point refers to a distance 100 diameters away from large massive objects. Try to activate a JumpDrive within that distance and things tend to go poorly.
The black static ships travel through when they hit the FTL drive. Usually ships spend 148+6d6 hours in Jump Space per Jump, regardless of the distance travelled, though some manufacturers have tweaked that number slightly. Exiting a SpaceCraft in Jump Space means death as the victim's atoms are torn apart. Messily. It is generally believed that the further one travels through Jump Space the more dangerous it is. Before TheIsolation ships were routinely jumping up to 6 Parsecs at a time and people were succumbing to a form of SpaceMadness that became codified as the ReaverPlague.

The KawzanIndustries JumpPod is a semi-modular starship designed for light transport and utility duties.  It is built on a 100dtn unstreamlined hull, equipped with short landing legs on the underside to allow landing on vacuum worlds, asteroids, hangar bays and other appropriate places.  The ship mounts jump drive A, maneuver drive A and power plant A giving a performance of Jump-2 and 2G acceleration.  Fuel tankage of 40dtns supports the power plant and allows one jump-2.

Adjacent to the bridge is a computer Model/1bis.  There is one stateroom and no low berths.  The ship has no hardpoints and no cargo capacity, but it does have a Module Bay that can accept a wide variety of 20dtn modules.

The Kawzan Industries Jump Pod requires a crew of one: the Pilot.  Up to one additional crewmember may be carried, requiring double occupancy, and more may be carried if a module with crew quarters is provided.

The ship costs MCr29.8 to build (including architect’s fees) and can be built in 9 months.  In quantity, examples of this ship can be built for MCr26.6.

Some examples of standard modules available for the Jump Pod include:
Fuel Module –- MCr1, provides 20dtns of additional fuel tankage.
Cargo Module –- MCr1, provides 20dtns of cargo in a pressure-tight compartment.
Habitat Module – MCr2, provides four staterooms, two tons of cargo and a self-contained power plant with fuel for four weeks of independent operations.
Launch – MCr14, this is a standard 20dtn Launch.

Area Descriptions
Main Deck

   1. Bridge – control center for the ship.  The command chair sits in an observation bubble forward, overlooking the bow.  A second control seat with engineering repeaters and communications gear is to starboard, as is a fresher.  There is an iris valve in the deck to port.  Port aft is the computer room, containing the main controls for the ship’s Model/1bis computer.
   2. Avionics Access Way – a tool rack is across from the entry door.  Some avionics equipment is present here, as is an iris valve to the avionics bay below.
   3. Crew Quarters – cramped living space for one or two crewmen.  Two bunks fold out of the wall in the port side area, a space also taken up by a compact galley.  A table and one or two chairs is in the middle of the space.  There is a small airlock to starboard, which opens on the dorsal surface of the ship.
   4. Locker – storage for food, some personal equipment and two vacc suits.
   5. Life Support – controls and equipment for recycling and environment maintenance.
   6. Main Engineering – jump and maneuver drives for the ship.  A hatch in the center of the deck leads to the power plant below, and a seldom-used hatch aft can be used for engineering work while the ship is in a hangar bay.  As with most engineering bays, the decking here consists of metal grids that can be pulled up in sections to access conduits and piping beneath the work area.

Lower Deck

   7. Avionics Bay – sensors, scanners, and other electronic gear for operating the ship. 
   8. Main Airlock – iris valves open from here to the Equipment Bay, the Module Bay, and to port.  A metal ladder can extend from the hull beneath this airlock for when the pod lands on an airless world or in a hangar, as the ship’s landing legs will keep the airlock about two meters above the landing surface.
   9. Equipment Bay – Large storage lockers, racks and shelves hold tools, spare parts, emergency equipment and other gear.
  10. Lower Engineering – an extension of Main Engineering above, this deck contains the ship’s power plant.
  11. Module Bay – this bay is open to space forward and below.  It has multiple grapples and connectors, allowing it to carry and use a variety of 20dtn modules.  The ship is shown carrying a 20dtn Launch in the bay; examples of some other possible pods are displayed as well.

 
Fuel Module

This module carries an additional 20dtns of fuel, with connectors allowing it to pump the fuel into the main tanks of the Jump Pod.  With a Fuel Module in place, it is possible for the Jump Pod to travel up to four parsecs without refueling.

 
Cargo Module

This module can carry up to 20dtns of cargo. 

  12. Cargo Bay -- a large cargo hatch opens forward, while an iris valve to port can mate up with the Jump Pod’s Main Airlock.  Note the small ladder down from the iris valve.
  13. Environmental Controls – machinery is provided here to maintain minimum environmental support to the pressure-tight Cargo Bay.  Long-term operation requires connection to the Jump Pod or other source of power; when not so connected, the machinery here can maintain minimum life support for only about two hours.

 
Habitat Module

This module is designed to provide living quarters for up to eight people.  It has short, adjustable landing legs and its own power plant, and can thus be landed at a site and will work independently for up to four weeks without resupply.

14.  Commons – kitchen, dining room, recreation area and workroom for the inhabitants of this module.  A compact galley is to port, and storage shelves line all walls.  An iris valve in the deck leads to the lower lever of the module, and an airlock opens to port.  This airlock can mate with the Jump Pod’s Main Airlock, and there is a ladder built-in to the outer hull of the module allowing inhabitants to climb the two meters down to the surface when the module is operating independently.

15.  Quarters – this passage leads past two crew cabins, each equipped with a storage locker, two foldaway bunks, a desk and a worktable.  A fresher and a storage closet are near the aft end of the passage, as is access to the Machinery Room.

16.  Machinery Room – this space contains the module’s power plant and some environmental controls.  Connection and monitoring equipment is also present, allowing the module to link power feeds up to the Jump Pod.

17.  Work Room – this space contains a worktable, communications and simple sensor controls, and equipment stores.  An iris valve in the deck above leads to the Commons.

18.  Bunkroom – This space contains four foldaway bunks and two large storage closets.  Additional storage space is available under the bunks, in containers that easily double as seating and work surfaces.  The Habitat Module’s small stock of fuel is located in a baffled tank just aft of this space.

Kamorr Subsector is a more backwards region than ChaifengSubsector. During the ColonialWar the systems here were hit with more ground warfare as the PrimaryWorlds attempted to solidify their hold on the food supplies they could provide to the front.

The main faction in the subsector is the VagabondWorlds. It is completely [[Jump2]] Accessible.

[[1090]] Came of age as a raider
[[1072]] born
Ally from TheShatters NunoRoque
Contact on LibertyStation NetunoZe

SkillTotal: 7

"I was born on a small colony world.  Which one, I'm not sure.  For you see, when I was only a year or two old, raiders nabbed me when they pilaged the town. 

"I was raised as one of them.  The raiders don't have the traditional "family" structure or values.  Not that I knew about such things till later in life.  I know what you're thinking.  Why bother taking kids?  They are smelly, noisy and would just gobble up all your food.  It's simple.  A matter of survival.  The raiders kidnap children because they're infertile.  Something to do with living near a radioactive star.  There are a few "lucky" raiders who had natural children.  Those kids almost always have some form of mutation, physical or mental.  Who knows if I'm capable of having children of my own.

I grew up a tinkerer.  I loved to take things apart to see how they worked. All my uncles and aunts didn't appreciate such talent untill I learned how to put things back together.  It started off with fixing toy cars and planes, working my way up to helping fix the raiding ships and weapons.  When I became of age, I joined a ships crew. 
 
But every child has to leave the nest.  Sometimes forcably.  I had been part of a few raids, but this one mining colony would change my life.  I've never hurt anyone myself, at least not too badly.  That didn't stop some miner from taking a shot at me.  Got me right in the guts.  Painfull as hell.  The only family I had know, the raiders, left me behind.  A casualty of thier lifestyle.  Our lifestyle.  The mining colony medics worked for hours saving my life.  When I recovered enough, I found out that I was the only surviving raider.   Saved only to be put on public display.  A target for the colonies anger.  I was judged, found guilty and sentenced as a slave to work in the mines. 
 
And so a new life began.  The work was rough.  The condition horrible.  The food even worse.  It didn't take the masters long to realize what an asset they had.  A fix-it!  Soon enough, I was fixing more than I was mining.  Can't mine if you don't have a machine to pump in the air.  Nothing really notable happened.  Escaped some close calls, a cave in or two.  Soon enough, the end of my sentence was in sight.
 
Till I was sold.  That's the problem with being a slave.  I was just about to end my sentence and be a free man.  Then the colony sold me off to some captain.  Now who know's what will happen?
 
Who am I?  I'm Kendrick "Scot" McNab.    Scot for my flaming red hair.  McNab, cause Uncle Ross found it ironic.  Who said raiders don't have a sence of humor.  I was nabbed, get it?  Oh never mind. . . 
KenzhouSystem 2030 B867967-10 N T P Ga Hi

18-year old woman raped and killed by YuriBudanov during the ChryssanCampaign in [[1100]].
One of LiberVaclaw's goons on [[Perdition]]. Got hit in the nuts then accidentally shot in the leg by TobiasFleet.
See KroAdministration
The Kro Administration spans multiple subsectors from its capital world [[Syganga]]. While they are human, somewhere along the line they developed psionic abilities. To a Kro it seems natural but the manipulation of matter and even it seems energy with these powers makes the PrimaryWorlders very very nervous. The habit of random worlds in long forgotten places "going Kro" makes them sweat even more.
The KroAdministration's navy has slightly more advanced technology than the PrimaryWorldsNavy. One obvious area is the new LymanDrive, which adds much more range to their longer Jump vessels. The Kro do tend to use Fission PowerPlants more as well, possibly due to the relative inexpense of radioactives in their systems.
The more seedy SpacePort on LibertyStation, but the one where no questions are asked. It isn't TransportPowers sanctioned and is part of the reason LibertySystem is declared an AmberZone.

The LamosianLimo as it's sometimes called, these TL7 designs are about the cheapest ways to get a handful of pirates onto a lightly defended ship. Usually the pirates are in Vacc suits for the inevitable decompression when they are fired upon. They have a short effective range but in a swarm they can stop an undergunned ship in its tracks. It is not unheard of for these little boats to carry nukes.

LamosSystem 1030 B561A7B-7 S T I P Hi RedZone

This oppressive, highly populated near-desert world in TheWilds is known throughout the sector more for the people who manage to leave it, the LamosianPirates. It was been involved in a murderous civil war since [[1087]] when the former dictator SiadBarre was overthrown by warlords.
Person from [[Lamos]]
The world of [[Lamos]] in TheWilds isn't a fun place to live. Some speculate that's why so many people leave as soon as they can. Emigration is strictly controlled and few ever return to their homeland. But Lamosians have made a name for themselves in the galaxy at large simply by stealing. They are the most active pirate group in TheEdgeofSpace. They aren't necessarily the most professional, but the blood ties and bonds of a shared homeland make the group, scattered as it is, nearly impossible for PrimaryWorlds counterterrorism agents to crack. The classification of Lamosian Pirates specifically as a terrorist group is something seen by many in the Edge as proof that the DownCore are soft pudgy doughpeople who would outlaw anything smacking of independent thought/pulling up by the bootstraps.

The HereWard-born Autrum is a 52 year old highly skilled, highly intelligent born leader who also has a problem with authority – especially Imperial authority. Autrum is dedicated to one ideal: his own empowerment. He believes that the Imperium is destined to fall because of its stagnation. His ideas are enthusiastically shared by the VagabondWorlds crew of DeepStrike, and Autrum will debate anyone who thinks the Imperium is a good idea until his opposition give up in intellectual exhaustion. It is hard to understand why such an expert on the Imperium is not lecturing at a radical university somewhere, but Autrum is also a sucker for money and riches, hence his highly lucrative privateering “business” – and his gambling problem. 

Autrum quickly rose to the position of captain in the HereWardPlanetaryNavy, demonstrating extraordinary skills as a bridge officer, tactician, navigator and pilot. But his passion for high roller gambling apparently led to his “retirement” from the HereWardPlanetaryNavy. Autrum is still in the Navy career because he is working for the HellSongPlanetaryNavy, albeit in an unusual 
capacity.

LibertySystem  2023  B300730-10 N S R T I Na Va A
Size/Gravity: 4800km 0.25G
Atmosphere: None
Surface Water: 3% (100% frozen)
Population: 6,000,000
Government: No central authority
!General Background
LibertyStation is a notoriously lawless haven for pirates and thieves, although much of notoriety comes from people who've never been there. 

LibertySystem plays an important buffer role between the FreeworldsCluster and the PioneerConfederation, since there is no suitable GasGiant for refuelling and the TransportPowers (who keep a number of bases in the system) have so many restrictions on FarHaulers which could bypass this cold cold world.
!Local Conditions
LibertyStation is frozen solid under its dim red sun. No atmosphere or surface moisture to speak of, and the entire mantle is superfrozen ice. Liberty has a 24 hour day, and a 2892.3 day year. Gravity is about 0.15G. There is a Mag1 magnetic field. It's orbited by FreedomMoon (14,400km distant) and DeathMoon (120,000km distant), two planetoidal bodies. Death is a small body that orbits every 125 hours. It is much larger than any of the stars, but not as large as the red sun. Freedom however is very close and occupies 3 degrees of sky in its 41.5 hour orbit.
!Major Population Centres
People who live on Liberty live in pressurized arcologies. Outside of the company mining towns the cities tend to be grim enclaves, held together in tight family units when machinery breaks down. Generations have been born here and they exhibit the more fragile bone structure common to low-gravity dwellers. There are genetic treatments available but anything beyond TL10 must come in from offworld.
!!StarPorts
!!!LibertyDirt
!!!LibertyFar
!!!KryptonDown
There used to be an actual Liberty Station. Its remnants are found in a series of craters on the planet's equator. Today there is a BeanStalk up to LibertyFar from LibertyDirt (the two parts to the StarPort; because of superstitions about the crashed LibertyStation no one refers to LibertyHigh or LibertyDown). The other main SpacePort on Liberty is known as KryptonDown. It deals with intrasystem trade and trafficking, and isn't under the control of the TransportPowers, so is often used for shadier dealings.

LibertyFar is home to a PrimaryWorlds Consulate for those who have urgent business. It was relocated up to the HighPort after the ColonialWar which made it a target for many people. The security around it is the heaviest one sees on Liberty.
!Local Law
Weapons: No restrictions
Drugs: No restrictions
Information: No restrictions
Technology: No restrictions
Offworlders: No restrictions
Psionics: No restrictions
Other: No restrictions
Liberty is run by a few wealthy barons who are in constant competition with each other. And by wealthy we mean obscenely rich. Happily for some, they don't do a lot of interfering in the day to day operations of the mining concerns. Nothing is restricted on Liberty. Some of the corporations have their own internal regulations but as long as TerraDyne and AnslemVirek get their cuts on the sales, all eyes are blind.

Of course, LibertyFar and LibertyDirt are a different story, being controlled and run by the TransportPowers. Either of those stations have a standard StarPort legality wherein AssaultWeapons, AddictiveNarcotics, SecurityPrograms and TL13 items are all restricted. Technically, every SpaceCraft should be docking at the StarPort but enough credits pass through enough hands to ensure that those laws are only enforced when it is convenient.

!Threats
Criminal/Pirate Activity: Moderate
War: Minimal
Radiation: Minimal
The Liberty System is huge and dark. The sun is a RedGiant which never developed a Jovian planet to shepherd many other bits of rock around, leaving a series of rocky planets and two Asteroid Clusters. LibertyStation isn't on the closest world to the sun, but 203 AU away, in the SuperFrigid zone. No one really knows why [[Fraternity]] ZetaTerran wasn't colonized long ago, as apart from the dryness it would make a near perfect world for settling. TerraDyne bought the exploration rights from PlanetXS to the world last year ([[1104]]) and now has a small survey crew on the planet making inquiries and plans. Many on LibertyStation dispute the legality of the exclusive nature of that deal with PlanetXS.

Most intrasystem travel is actually undertaken by microjump since LibertyStation is so far out in the system. It would take a year to get to the TheShatters AsteroidBelt from LibertyStation otherwise. There is a StarPort on a large planetoid in TheShatters called EqualityStation. Currently TheShatters region is the home to a large scale infestation of LamosianPirates, engaged in a number of ransom negotiations.

Ling Standard Products ([[LSP]]) currently engages in a wide spectrum of activities including (but by no means limited to) manufacture of electronic equipment of all sorts, ground and air vehicles, starships and starship armaments systems, drive systems, power systems, computer systems and software, small arms, and a variety of other items.

Concerned to a small degree with banking, insurance, and other activities, LSP maintains mining and manufacturing facilities throughout the Imperium and beyond.

LSP began as a mining and mineral exploitation firm (and is still very active in that area). Later it expanded into manufacturing to create markets for its raw materials. It now transports raw materials and finished goods within the PrimaryWorlds and approximately 20 parsecs beyond the Imperial borders.

Interests: Mining, electronics, vehicles, weapons, consumer goods.

Stock ownership: ImperialFamily, 8%; HortalezEtCie, 26%; GSbAG, 23%; MurdochHoldings LIC , 8%; Noble families, 8%; Other, 27%.

Financial institution with close ties to KawzanIndustries on [[Fantomas]]. From [[1090]]-[[1096]] it employed GuntherLockhart. It was attacked in [[1093]] as part of the beginning of the ColonialWar.
The LonelyRoad is an X-Class Jump 2 traderoute between [[Glitter]] and the KroAdministration. It requires a large fuel capacity and the capability to collect fuel along the way, but there are independent traders who take this path. Instead of Jumping to [[Fluxxus]] it is also possible to go to [[Syganga]]. If that is the case the only benefit of the LonelyRoad over the PioneerRoute is that it takes you through barren systems where meeting another soul is unlikely. This is good for smugglers and those who'd rather their voyages into non-Alliance territory weren't publicized. It is the fastest Jump 2 route to [[Shipsend]].

Under standard procedure, preparing a passenger for low passage takes 1-6 hours and requires the presence of a medic (but no task roll). Reviving a low passenger is a Medic, Endurance, 1-6 hours, Easy (+4) task using the passenger's Endurance DM. In both cases one medic could simultaneously work on up to 20 low berths, but the medic has to make a separate task roll for each passenger he or she attempts to revive. A failed revival roll results in 3d6 normal damage rather than instant death. Healthy low passengers frozen and revived using the standard procedure rarely die, but might need prompt medical attention in some cases; infirm, ill or wounded passengers are at greater risk.

In emergencies, however, it is possible to quickly freeze a character, taking only 10-60 seconds and not requiring any medic to be present. This emergency procedure is automatic and may even be initiated by the passenger himself by using an override switch inside the low berth. Reviving a passenger frozen in this manner is subject to a -2 DM.

It is also possible to quickly revive a low passenger using the emergency revival procedure, which is a Medic, Endurance, 1-6 minutes, Average (+0) task using the passenger's Endurance DM. This could either be done by a medic or by triggering an override failsafe mechanism of the low berth (which is treated as if it had Medic 0 for this purpose). A failed emergency revival task causes a roll on the Injury table (TMB p.37); damage is permanent unless treated in a hospital of TL10 or better (using the costs listed on TMB p.37).
Low Technology worlds are pre-industrial and cannot produce advanced goods on their own.

The Lyman Drive was developed by the advanced research facility on [[Taisto]], though it is somewhat different than the TaistoDrive. There are rumours that in a fit of pique at the lack of licensability of the LymanDrive under TransportPowers regulations the facility sold the technology to the KroAdministration as a way to fund their real projects. When [[Taisto]] was destroyed in the opening days of the ColonialWar that seemed to put an end to the drive, though PrimaryWorlds researchers are beginning to see the Lyman Drive as a viable alternative for the future. No mass production has begun in the PrimaryWorlds on LymanDrive ships yet.
!Specifications
The Lyman Drive requires more fuel for a Jump-1 than a standard Jump Drive, but the fuel requirements for higher jumps are significantly lower - a Jump-6 requires less than 15% of hull to be allocated to fuel carriage/storage. The fuel usage figures depend on jump range and tech level of construction, and are as follows:

FarHauler CargoShip from [[Endeavour]]. Hijacked in LibertySystem on [[1105-029]]. It had been bringing [[Petrochemicals]] from [[Syganga]] back to [[Chaifeng]].
Established in 1040 with an Imperial charter and a mineral exploitation grant for Fulacin ( Rhylanor / Spinward Marches 2613). The corporation holds several patents for the recovery of precious and heavy metals from atmospheric and oceanic suspension, and originally obtained its position on Fulacin for the use of these properties.

Following the severe economic downturn associated with the False War (1082 to 1084), the company encountered a cash slowdown, and suspended operations for a period. In 1089, an influx of capital allowed the company to resume operations. In partial support of this new era, the company also established a large starport facility (currently class A minus ) with construction and overhaul facilities to 10,000 tons. The starport was completed in 1099.

MagnetoDynamics' exploration grant expires in 1199, with a renewability clause for an additional 100 years upon demonstration of efficient and profitable operations.

Stock Ownership: Spinward nobility, 8%; Imperial Family, 2%; large corporations, 34%; investment trusts, 46%; public (individuals), 8%.

Str 2d6 Dex 1d6 End 3d6 Instinct 1d6 HP 2d6 Roll d6 when killed: 1-2 get up again. Bite 1d6 damage (on a 6 armour reduced by 1) failed End check: contracts the disease 1d6 dmg/hour.
Port facility for the support, maintenance , repair and refit of naval vessels. Made up of several distinct parts, the typical ImperialNavy base is comprised of an orbital berthing area, a surface berthing area, a maintenance section, and an administrative headquarters.

Berthing areas provide locations for ships to lay over, whether for a day or for months. Planetary surface facilities are generally provided for vessels of 1000 tons or less; orbital facilities handle larger ships. All berthing areas include provisions for refuelling from storage tanks or fuel lighters.

Maintenance sections vary from base to base. Where such a section would be redundant to the local shipyard, it is small, and repairs or alterations are carried out under contract to the local facility. Where adequate facilities do not exist, the naval base itself may have a large maintenance section capable of extensive repairs and refits. Maintenance is performed on the ships on the world surface or in orbit as necessary.

The administrative headquarters handles the day-to-day operations of the base as well as the paperwork, including allocation of funds, distribution of personnel, and disbursement of maintenance and repair contracts.

The naval base is not a tactical unit. It has no battle forces of its own, and does not exert control even over local SDBs (which are under a separate command). The naval base is responsible for supporting the fleet and keeping it in optimum shape for its combat missions.

Nuno was a [[Freed]] worker in the mines with KendrickMcNab. They were close friends and recently he decided to leave the mining life behind and is working on the BestofIntentions an OberlindesLines SuperFreighter.
Oberlindes Lines is an interface line trading between TheAlliance and the KroAdministration in SectorEDG-7913. It is the major shipping company in ChaifengSubsector, and operates the only SuperFreighter working this far out on TheEdge.

The Oberlindes name is an old one in the trade and commerce business in TheEdge. RoxanneOberlindes established the first line to bear the name in [[0487]], and built up a large family business from a free trader operation. The company thrived between each of the several wars which have wracked TheEdge in the past half-millennium.

The first major increase in Oberlindes' size came in [[1064]] with the acquisition of TheEmissary, an AzhantiHighLightningClass FrontierCruiser declared surplus by the AllianceNavy. This ship, armaments intact, served as the flagship for Oberlindes' excusions into the KroExtents on trade expeditions; the venture proved highly successful. A base was established just beyond the Imperial border (some irregularities in the ship transfer made it impractical to bring the ship into Alliance territory) and served as a clearing house for trade good shipments between [[Chaifeng]] and the worlds of the KroAdministration.

Following the FourthFrontierWar ([[1084]]), the company obtained an ImperialCharter and naval surplus transports. They used them to provide extensive cargo service in the ChaifengSubsector, concentrating on the smaller feeder routes. This proved to be most lucrative, as worlds cut off by the fighting had a high demand for trade goods. At the same time, Oberlindes expanded into trade with the KroAdministration just beyond the Imperial border, and has become a major importer of [[Kro]] products and goods. 

The line has expanded into main line service, with a GPSuperFreighter running in direct competition with TukeraLines and other established major shipping lines on the HellSong-Syganga route. Expansion into neighbouring subsectors has improved interstellar service for travellers, but has alienated many of the older and more conservative lines.

MarcHautOberlindes, patriarch and controller of the line, was awarded a baronial patent, complete with estates on [[Luxin]], by direction of the Emperor in [[1101]]. The patent was in recognition of his contribution to economic recovery in TheEdgeofSpace following the FourthFrontierWar. His heir apparent is his son, SergeiHautOberlindes. Sergei was recently ([[1104]]) rescued from imprisonment on [[Glitter]].

Home Port: [[Chaifeng]]

Territory: ChaifengSubsector and KamorrSubsector; SygangaSubsector.

Current Owner: MarcHautOberlindes. Stock Ownership: Oberlindes family, 78%; ImperialFamily, 2%; corporate employees, 8%; investment trusts, 10%; public (individuals), 2%.

Current Fleet: the commercial fleet consists of more than 100 ships, which includes TheEmissary (an AzhantiHighLightningClass FrontierCruiser), the BestofIntentions (a GPSuperFreighter), 9 other ships of greater than 4000 tons and 30 other ships of greater than 1000 tons. Many of their small ships out in TheEdge are WerimazhClass.

OnoSendai specializes in manufacturing complex electronic devices. These include robots, computers, and information storage and processing equipment, plus the associated software. It is the primary supplier of communication equipment to the ExpressBoatService, a branch of PlanetXS. OnoSendai is also involved in transport operations, concentrated in the Alliance's rimward areas.

OnoSendai is the largest robot manufacturer in the Alliance. Its robots rarely use innovative technology, but their aggressive marketing staff has placed more robots than either TyrrellCorp or [[LSP]], OnoSendai's two largest competitors. Old Sendai introduced the [[Rashush]] line of robots, the first non-military line, 200 years after the Rule of Manwas established. It is still marketed today. OnoSendai retails a standard model TL15 servant robot with INT 5 and an EDU 1 for Cr77,500. Its useful life is 85 years.

Interests: Information retrieval hardware and software, robots, electronics.

Home Port: Tauri ( Vland / Vland 1817).

Stock ownership: ImperialFamily, 5%; IgsiirdiFamily, 13%; HortalezEtCie, 11%; investment trusts, 24%; noble families, 23%; other corporations, 14%; private, 11%.

AlMorai - ArkeshSpacers - BaraccaiTechnum - BilsteinYards - CAMInterstellar - DaihatsuNova - [[Dzofakael]] - KawzanIndustries - LonCorp - MagnetoDynamics - MercyGeneral - OberlindesLines - OnoSendai - SeaHarvester - SinzarmesDirect - TyrrellCorp - VersiStar - LexCorp - PrimaTech - BlueSun - MerrickBiotech - FatboyIndustries - BuyNLarge - VeidtIndustries - WeylandYutani - CyberdyneSystems - YoyoDyne - OmniConsumerProducts - GeneCo -
InterstellarTrade is regulated and taxed by the PrimaryWorlds. This provides an incentive to organize in evading tariffs and smuggling illegal-to-trade goods. That's the basis for most large scale criminal conspiracies in TheEdgeofSpace. Here we are talking about more than simple one-ship pirate bands with a loose affiliation beholden to no one, but actual organizations with a broader hierarchy and mandate.

1) The most basic business of such an organization is dealing in goods that are:
* Low volume, highly valuable, highly taxed.
* Illegal for import on a particular world (drugs, weapons, etc.).
* Illegal or restricted for trade in general (slaves, pirated merchandise, military-grade equipment, Ancient artifacts).
2) Territory consists of routes between worlds.

3) Small ship owners would be prime recruits for low level membership, with high rewards for compliance and threats for the obstinate. This results in all small ship owners living under a cloud of suspicion, since everyone knows they are prime recruits!

4) Money laundering is more difficult on high technology worlds, but it will be these worlds most attractive to spend one's ill-gotten gains. The solution might be to fund "trade" with a world where there is poor record keeping as a cover for profits.

5) Bonds of blood and culture are useful in ensuring loyalty. A crime syndicate might grow from a particular minority who dislike cooperating with authorities and have few options other than crime. (See LamosianPirates and their breakaway group the EthuengPirates.)

6) In some frontier regions fighting such an organization is yet another job foisted off on PlanetXS, as their Scouts are used to operating in small groups or singularly over a vast section of space.
See AveryOzzum

PerditionSystem 1819 X798204-3 S Ga Lo Lt
!Background
Perdition is Rimward edge of the FreeworldsCluster. It's not on the HellSong-Syganga trade corridor so it's left pretty much alone. The tiny population (~600) means not many people get to enjoy the planets clear skies and bright red nights.
!Local Conditions
0.9G, Temperate climate. 24 hour days. 1093 day year. Axial tilt of 10 degrees so the seasonal variation isn't incredibly severe. JumpPoint 1.12million km distant. DeltaEujovian 480million km distant.
!Starport
Perdition doesn't have a StarPort or SpacePort. Ships coming to trade simply find a bit of open area to land in near the main settlement. The JumpPoint is about 1,000,000 km from the planet.
!Society and Law
Perdition is settled by a few hundred people without a clear government. In the (550ish day) summer they're scattered across the world hunting [[Uniac]], but in the winter they congregate into a few main settlements. Since the clans' manufacturing capabilities cannot handle advanced technology of any sort, imports are used to maintain the colony at a comfortable level. Weapons more advanced than pistols are discouraged by all the families as the medical treatment available means horrible deaths for anyone involved in such a fight. At least there's a chance for their medics against slug throwers. Also, energy rifles and the like wouldn't be useful in [[Uniac]] hunting, as they would damage the wool beyond value.

As of early [[1105]] LiberVaclaw is the big man in Town. Every few months a TravellingMagistrate will come in from [[Piety]] to settle any disputes that've gotten out of hand so murdering won't happen.
!Characters
LiberVaclaw Broker - MortonQuintos [[Uniac]] Poacher - ErikaDell [[Uniac]] Hunter
!Economy
Perdition mainly relies on supplies from [[Piety]]. Since the population is so low and there's no spaceport, none of the big transport corporations have it as a stop on their routes. LiberVaclaw has an associate on [[Piety]], PavlinaDari, who arranges for supply trips from small freighters.
!!!Export Goods
CommonGoods - BasicRawMaterials +2 - BasicConsumables +1 - LiveAnimals ([[Uniac]]) +0 - LuxuryConsumables ([[Uniac]] Wool) +0 - [[Spices]] +0 - [[Wood]] +0 - IllegalLuxuries ([[Uniac]] Organs) +0
!!!Import Goods
BasicElectronics +1 - LiveAnimals (Horses) +3 - PetroChemicals +2 - [[Pharmaceuticals]] +1
Perdition orbits a binary star system, a normal sun plus a RedDwarf.
